  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_587b97af-6eb6-48cf-ab1c-a3e4e0ee356c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer1248613541915003328">When a 16 year old, small town girl, Christine Matthews, from Dryden, Michigan gets a shot at playing semi- professional hockey on a boys hockey team she jumps at the opportunity.<br/><br/>Follow her ups and downs as she tackles some of lives hardships, surprises, and victories as she reaches out to catch her dreams. Journey with her as she struggles through some of life's tough sit</span>
  <span id="freeText1248613541915003328" style="display:none">When a 16 year old, small town girl, Christine Matthews, from Dryden, Michigan gets a shot at playing semi- professional hockey on a boys hockey team she jumps at the opportunity.<br /><br />Follow her ups and downs as she tackles some of lives hardships, surprises, and victories as she reaches out to catch her dreams. Journey with her as she struggles through some of life's tough situations, as well as love and loss.Her story is inspirational to people every where who feel their dreams are unreachable. <br /><br />Christine wants one thing in her life, hockey. Nothing would ever mean more to her than that. She had worked so hard for it without the support of her friends and family. When she meets Alex her world starts to change. <br /><br />Why was she so enticed by this boy. She had to stop thinking about how gorgeous he was. He would be running for the exits as soon as he found out what she was doing there. She noticed that her palms were starting to sweat, she wiped them on her jeans, before he noticed. She wanted to hate him. She couldn't have these type of distractions around her. She needed to be focused on the prize.<br /><br />Then there was Moose. What would she do without him? This couldn't be happening right now, not to her. She still had her stalker to deal with. The hatred he had for her, in those deep black coal eyes. Was her life about to spiral out of control?</span>

<div id="review_467886470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467886470" />
    <a title="Jami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10155422-jami"><img alt="Jami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339464661p2/10155422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467886470?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jami" href="/user/show/10155422-jami">Jami</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10155422-jami?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer467886470&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467886470" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10814161732894673639">So this will probably be the only book on my Did not finish shelf. I finish everything. I mean everything. But I just really can't read another word. First of the typos. I understand that no one is perfect and especially when you add the headache of an e-book transfer. But wow. The grammar and spelling errors are just atrocious. "Breath" for "breathe", "starred" for "stared", wrong tenses, etc. This author doesn't have one friend she could give her manuscript to for editing? It might have caught</span>
  <span id="freeText10814161732894673639" style="display:none">So this will probably be the only book on my Did not finish shelf. I finish everything. I mean everything. But I just really can't read another word. First of the typos. I understand that no one is perfect and especially when you add the headache of an e-book transfer. But wow. The grammar and spelling errors are just atrocious. "Breath" for "breathe", "starred" for "stared", wrong tenses, etc. This author doesn't have one friend she could give her manuscript to for editing? It might have caught most of these glaring errors.<br /><br />But if we overlook the errors, which I did for the most part, and focus on the story here's where it's just really insane. So this girl is apparently a super great hockey player who never has to work harder than any of her male teammates. Okay, suspend disbelief. And then, when she wants to be, she's supermodel gorgeous and all the guys on the team want to date her. Uh huh. Wish fulfillment book. And I tried to move on from all that. And I did. Until I got to the group sex. Oh, yes. In a Young Adult novel. Group. Sex. With teenagers. <br /><br />What are y'all doing up there in Canada, anyway?! And this is normal for every guy on the team. Except for Alex who claims he's not into it. But what he is into is trying to have sex with a semi-conscious drunk girl on a couch. She ignored the offer of a ride home with her SOBER Captain who lives with her in their host family's home to get a ride home with a drunk womanizer instead. It's cool though. It's Canada, so no normal rules apply. <br /><br />All these guys apparently also have steady girlfriends but Chrissy respects them all so she'll never tell on them for cheating outrageously at these group sex parties. Yeah, okay. You're a falling down drunk cheater who participates in orgies and I am virgin. But I totally respect you. <br /><br />And still I tried to keep moving. Just keep plowing through. Until I got to the naked locker room set-up. Yep. Hockey wunderkind Chrissy just wants to be one of the guys. So now she's going to get dressed and shower with them so she'll be accepted. And the coach says okay! Now that everyone in this novel has lost their freaking mind I don't need to read anymore. Harassment lawsuit, anyone? Sexual assault? The possibility for some jerk teammate to take cell phone photos of her and post them online? No one seems to care. Not even the coaches and the captain who are supposed to protect her. Seems like she needs to be protected from her own stupidity more than anything.<br /><br />No respected Coach of ANY team would let something like this happen. The PR/legal risk is HUGE and there is no reward for anyone here. No one is going to like her more. No one is going to accept her more. At least not in the real world. <br /><br />So yeah, I'm not bothering to finish this one. I wish I could get my money back. I think it's odd that in all the reviews I read, no one mentioned 'group sex.' If they had I would have known this book had no basis in reality and I would not have bought it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10814161732894673639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237388563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237388563" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6333824-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451437719p2/6333824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237388563?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/6333824-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6333824-emily?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237388563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6015168677187969144">Oh boy. Where do I begin? I found the idea for this novel interesting, but it was very poorly written. There were grammar and spelling mistakes that are really third grade mistakes, and I don't know whether to put it to being the e-book version or not, but I don't think so. There were phrases too, that I couldn't believe were in there! It really was written like someone fresh out of junior high or something. <br/><br/>First off, the timeline, after her first year with the Gophers, made no sense. It was ju</span>
  <span id="freeText6015168677187969144" style="display:none">Oh boy. Where do I begin? I found the idea for this novel interesting, but it was very poorly written. There were grammar and spelling mistakes that are really third grade mistakes, and I don't know whether to put it to being the e-book version or not, but I don't think so. There were phrases too, that I couldn't believe were in there! It really was written like someone fresh out of junior high or something. <br /><br />First off, the timeline, after her first year with the Gophers, made no sense. It was jumping and skipping around, and one of my biggest pet peeves when reading is not being able to wrap my head around the timeline. When Chrissy and Alex were broken up, Chrissy said something about them being broken up for almost a year, but the way the book was written, for it to make sense, it really would have only been a few months. So if the author really meant a year, then it needed to be more clear. <br /><br />So Chrissy made it clear in the beginning of the novel that she wanted to focus on hockey, and hockey only. So how come every guy she came across (especially the ones on her team) she commented on how good-looking or cute they were? She even stated that she had never been this way before, but when she got to Toronto that's all she seemed to notice, was how good-looking guys were. I mean, maybe her teenage hormones began to kick in at that exact moment, but it still seemed like a little much. As an 18 year old girl, I don't comment THAT much on guys. <br /><br />I also get that she was out of the house and living on her own, but her parents just letting her fly off to Aruba for a week with a guy, when she's 17? Pigs would fly before my parents let me do that, and I'm out of the house as well. <br /><br />Something else that bothered me was that the last, gosh I don't know, 100 pages or so, <i>nothing happened.</i> Literally. Nothing. It just talked about her career, and maybe one or two things were thrown in there about her and Alex's relationship. But other than that, there was nothing going on. I don't know how I made it through it, because I almost need something to be constantly happening. Also, when I read the synopsis of this novel, it made it seem like the stalker issue was bigger than it actually was. He appeared two times before Moose attacked him with a baseball bat (which, by the way, if someone hits someone else in the head with a heavy item such as a BASEBALL BAT, and hits them in said head hard enough for blood to spatter on the wall, I'm pretty sure that that person would fall to the ground unconscious, not be able to climb out a window and travel some distance) and then he was caught by the police, and admitted what he was doing and why he was doing it. Come on, throw a little more drama into the mix! <br /><br />Things were described (like her bubble baths) in extreme detail, and then nothing would happen. I guess what I'm used to is when something is described in great detail, that something dramatic is about to happen. But no. It seemed to be described for the hell of it. <br /><br />Also, for her complaining about her being a "girl playing a guys sport" everything seemed to come pretty damn easy to her. She got on the CHL, and was accepted by the Gophers fairly easily. Once she stood up to the douche bag coach who wouldn't let her play on Team USA because she was a girl, she got on there and everything that way came easy to her. Then she was drafted to the NHL like that *snaps fingers* and I don't really remember anyone giving her a hard time. There was the coach, and then the stalker dude but both of those things last less than ten pages. <br /><br />It gets two stars because it kind of kept my attention, and the story line was interesting enough. It was just poorly written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6015168677187969144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1591306462854140557">This could have been good. This could have been really good.<br/><br/>But the grammar and spelling errors were just...it was atrocious. You can't make it through a paragraph without finding at least one.<br/><br/>The tone was that of a juvenile and while the girl is young, it was just too much "tell" and not enough "show" and she just came off as an arrogant brat to me. The pacing was ridiculously fast for important parts and then agonizingly slow for scenes like Chrissy getting dressed/putting up her hair/etc.<br/><br/>And </span>
  <span id="freeText1591306462854140557" style="display:none">This could have been good. This could have been really good.<br /><br />But the grammar and spelling errors were just...it was atrocious. You can't make it through a paragraph without finding at least one.<br /><br />The tone was that of a juvenile and while the girl is young, it was just too much "tell" and not enough "show" and she just came off as an arrogant brat to me. The pacing was ridiculously fast for important parts and then agonizingly slow for scenes like Chrissy getting dressed/putting up her hair/etc.<br /><br />And the sexism was pretty high, considering the whole plot is about a girl getting to play in the boys' league.<br /><br />It got really hard to look past the horrendous grammar/spelling/punctuation. I hope that the author has someone read over it and a rewrite is done. The story is promising, but the execution was butchered.</span>

<div id="review_515491253" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/515491253" />
    <a title="Gemma Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16751732-gemma-riley"><img alt="Gemma Riley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/515491253?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gemma Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gemma Riley" href="/user/show/16751732-gemma-riley">Gemma Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer515491253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5403787696910463009">I enjoy reading books by first time novelists. There is a first time for everyone and for most they are full of bad reviews. For Indie writers and self published authors, it's worse. I love reading their novels because it's like breathing new life into a dull market. I believe it's the trends that kill me. One vampire series does great and a million writers follow hoping for their books or series to hit it big. It becomes about the money. <br/><br/>This novel has not been properly edited. That is obvious </span>
  <span id="freeText5403787696910463009" style="display:none">I enjoy reading books by first time novelists. There is a first time for everyone and for most they are full of bad reviews. For Indie writers and self published authors, it's worse. I love reading their novels because it's like breathing new life into a dull market. I believe it's the trends that kill me. One vampire series does great and a million writers follow hoping for their books or series to hit it big. It becomes about the money. <br /><br />This novel has not been properly edited. That is obvious from the start. This original story is refreshing to read. I really loved that fact that it was different from anything out there. It's also nice to see a young girl who goes after what she wants and doesn't let others get in her way. It's the type of young adult book I don't mind that my daughter reads. Some of the smut these young girls read today sickens me. At least the main character in this novel has principals and not out there competing with other girls to sleep me guys. I read one of my daughters novels a while back the name escapes me now but it was basically about two girls who compete to sleep with the most guys in a summer. Let's just say we had to have a talk after I read that one. Books like Ice in my Veins are enlightening . <br /><br />It was a great one day read. I read it on the bus going to and from work and it entertained me. I can over look the typos and spelling mistakes. I make lots of them on a daily basis. <br /><br />I love to read and have tried to write in the past and it's just not in the cards for me. I commend this first time author for her courage to put herself out there to be critized. I feel it's important to support first timers. Also it's good to read poorly written books once in a while. If you don't then how can you appreciate the masterpieces.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5403787696910463009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_469439588" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469439588" />
    <a title="Ashley Jessip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15156116-ashley-jessip"><img alt="Ashley Jessip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354606754p2/15156116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469439588?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Jessip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Jessip" href="/user/show/15156116-ashley-jessip">Ashley Jessip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469439588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17433803259532253834">I really loved this book. As an ex of an OHL hockey player this book is closer to reality than many people might think. When I was dating my boyfriend girls stalked him all the time. They stalked me and wrote terrible things about me on the internet hoping he would break up with me. As for the group sex - it really happens in the hockey world. It's part of the sport. It's horrible that it happens but that is the main reason my relationship ended. I don't know any hockey player in the OHL that ha</span>
  <span id="freeText17433803259532253834" style="display:none">I really loved this book. As an ex of an OHL hockey player this book is closer to reality than many people might think. When I was dating my boyfriend girls stalked him all the time. They stalked me and wrote terrible things about me on the internet hoping he would break up with me. As for the group sex - it really happens in the hockey world. It's part of the sport. It's horrible that it happens but that is the main reason my relationship ended. I don't know any hockey player in the OHL that hasn't at one time cheated in their relationship. Girls send them pictures and videos of themselves doing disgusting things. The guys egos are so huge that they feel they can do whatever they want and get away with it. It was nice to see that the main character in this story had morals. I completely understand her not wanting to rat her teamates out because as a girlfriend of a player I was often put in that position. It was hard because my boyfriend told me things in confidence and even if I knew the girl who was being cheated on I felt I couldn't say anything. When I found out what really happens on the road with the guys and at their parties that the girlfriends aren't invited to I threw up. I couldn't continue my relationship. I know a few girls who do play on guy's team and my heart goes out to what they have to go through. I think this book is great although some of the chapters could have been explored in more detail it was a good read. I recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17433803259532253834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3350039166117041860">I picked up this book because some of the girls I know were discussing it and it sounded interesting and different. I wasn't disappointed. I debated about what rating to give this book because I would have liked the story to continue on into a second book. The story itself was wonderful. I find it extremely hard to related to my father like sh</span>
  <span id="freeText3350039166117041860" style="display:none">I picked up this book because some of the girls I know were discussing it and it sounded interesting and different. I wasn't disappointed. I debated about what rating to give this book because I would have liked the story to continue on into a second book. The story itself was wonderful. This is the reason for my 5 star rating. <br /><br />I could so relate to the relationship Chrissy has with her family. I also feel like the black sheep of my family. I find it extremely hard to related to my father like she does. Her father is so much like mine it was scary. <br /><br />Although the book is written around a female hockey player, hockey is not what the book really brings home. I felt with this character as she battled against each brick wall. I love that she's such a headstrong girl. When the writer talks about the sex going on around Chrissy and how it really bothers her I can totally relate. So many girls I know jump when a hot guy says how high. I loveeeeeee that she isn't like that. She kind of does have ice in her veins because she's so stubborn and headstrong. She puts up huge walls around her and almost loses out on love because of these walls. She's a smart driven girl who has a sarcastic nature to her. You can't help but fall in love with her. <br /><br />I think it's a great book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3350039166117041860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_755551434" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/755551434" />
    <a title="Jac (For Love and Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5908402-jac-for-love-and-books"><img alt="Jac (For Love and Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311899067p2/5908402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/755551434?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jac (For Love and Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jac (For Love and Books)" href="/user/show/5908402-jac-for-love-and-books">Jac (For Love and Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer755551434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2371349387267512839">**3.5 Stars**<br/><br/>I'm on a sports kick lately with my books, and especially into girls playing hockey!! (Perhaps because I'm spending 3 days a week at the ice arena with my daughter!) So Ice in my Veins was particularly appealing. <br/><br/>I struggled with my thoughts on this book for quite awhile. I was torn between feeling inspired and feeling frustrated. And in the end, I enjoyed the story more than the negative aspects. <br/><br/>Christine has to overcome a lot in this book. Her passion is hockey, and her family is</span>
  <span id="freeText2371349387267512839" style="display:none">**3.5 Stars**<br /><br />I'm on a sports kick lately with my books, and especially into girls playing hockey!! (Perhaps because I'm spending 3 days a week at the ice arena with my daughter!) So Ice in my Veins was particularly appealing. <br /><br />I struggled with my thoughts on this book for quite awhile. I was torn between feeling inspired and feeling frustrated. And in the end, I enjoyed the story more than the negative aspects. <br /><br />Christine has to overcome a lot in this book. Her passion is hockey, and her family isn't exactly supportive. (Because she's a girl.) They've told her flat out they'd be more supportive if she was into figure skating or gymnastics, but she's driven to be the best at hockey. She puts herself out there and gets a try-out with a Men's team in Canada (basically like triple A baseball - the farm team to a farm team...) Her story is incredibly inspiring, and despite all their flaws? So are the guys on her team! You can't help but love them.<br /><br />Kelli Sullivan has a strong story, for the first half of the book. Unfortunatly? After about the halfway point it really feels like an info dump. We follow Christine into middle age, which to me is too much. Starting with a 16 year old and following her until her own children are half grown?? Too much to fit into one book! <br /><br />And I can't write this review without addressing the grammar and spelling. It's as if there was ZERO editing - not even a reread - on this book. An example that sticks with me? Fanominally instead of Phenomenally. (And that's just one of many.) So with better editing alone? This book would have easily been better. <br /><br />In the end, this was a great story - worth the read. I read it in an afternoon, so I was definitely hooked to see what happened. The author did a fantastic job of showing the dark and dirty side of hockey - the infidelity, the sexism, the partying. She stayed true to her characters, and overall had an enjoyable story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2371349387267512839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9589025-mia-hastings?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9589025-mia-hastings?shelf=surprisingly-interesting">surprisingly-interesting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9589025-mia-hastings?shelf=breath-of-fresh-air">breath-of-fresh-air</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331550965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16254766476794074517">I loved..loved...loved, this book. I had read some good and bad reviews about this book. Once again I am so glad I didn't let the reviews effect deciding to read this book. I think this was a completely different sort of book. It was very realistic. I read one review that mentioned that at 17 the girls parents wouldn't let her go away. She must not play any competative sports. It's a requirement that your kid be able to travel - sometimes out of the country to play or compete. Also in my high sc</span>
  <span id="freeText16254766476794074517" style="display:none">I loved..loved...loved, this book. I had read some good and bad reviews about this book. Once again I am so glad I didn't let the reviews effect deciding to read this book. I think this was a completely different sort of book. It was very realistic. I read one review that mentioned that at 17 the girls parents wouldn't let her go away. She must not play any competative sports. It's a requirement that your kid be able to travel - sometimes out of the country to play or compete. Also in my high school at 17 most kids are seniors and everyone who is anyone takes the senior class trip to Cuba or Cancun. <br /><br />I loved that Chrissy wasn't afraid to be herself and to stand up for herself. I think it's an important lesson for many of my girlfriends. I have friend who believes she has to pretend she's a dumbass in order to be liked. She's afraid of what people think of her. As for the sex in this story - well if you have ever been to a high school party things like that happen all the time. I don't do it but so many of my classmates did. It's a very different world than our parents grew up in. Sex is so open now. I was one of the last of my group of friends to loss my virginity and was constantly teased because of it. There is a lot of pressure now a days to have sex before you are ready. It was refreshing to see her wait until she was ready.<br /><br />I think this story is a wonderful story for any girl/woman to read. It's very inspirational to see a girl work so hard and be so strong. I recommend this book to any reader.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16254766476794074517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_499699475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/499699475" />
    <a title="Phanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13943091-phanessa"><img alt="Phanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600833305p2/13943091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/499699475?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phanessa" href="/user/show/13943091-phanessa">Phanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13943091-phanessa?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer499699475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15401716335735833133">I was so hopeful for this book - so very, very hopeful for this book - because it's about a girl that plays hockey and wants to play it professionally. I love hockey, I am a girl that plays hockey, granted, I will never have the dream to be a pro because I only played for two years in college and it's the funniest sight you'd ever see, me on skates, but I just love the thought of a girl having this impossible dream and working on her way to achieve it.<br/><br/>Now, like I said, I was just so hopeful for </span>
  <span id="freeText15401716335735833133" style="display:none">I was so hopeful for this book - so very, very hopeful for this book - because it's about a girl that plays hockey and wants to play it professionally. I love hockey, I am a girl that plays hockey, granted, I will never have the dream to be a pro because I only played for two years in college and it's the funniest sight you'd ever see, me on skates, but I just love the thought of a girl having this impossible dream and working on her way to achieve it.<br /><br />Now, like I said, I was just so hopeful for this book but it let me down. Four stars just for the female hockey player alone. But once I saw 'phenomenal' spelled wrong, I new that this would not be a Five star book for me. And then there was the whole romance aspect to it and how it just seemed thrown in there just for more story. It was too forced. Along with the bullying. I understand that not everyone is going to accept her as a lone girl on a men's team, I've dealt with men in hockey myself, it just seemed to forced.<br /><br />After reading a few reviews about the behind the scenes aspect of hockey and puck sluts and bunnies and after meeting a few myself, I completely agree with all of that. Was it easy to read in this, not even in the slightest.<br /><br />All in all, it's a good book, really. There were just a few problems that could have been handled differently.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15401716335735833133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Dana Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6103793-dana-martin"><img alt="Dana Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314062860p2/6103793.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15125342515127020093">This book would have been good, WOULD HAVE BEEN, if a red pen had ever gone to the manuscript. This was clearly a self published book, and an unedited self published book at that. The plot was okay, and I only finished it because I liked the subject matter. I find there's not enough books that revolve around hockey which is what drew me to this book. To be honest I felt like I was reading the first "novel" I ever tried to write. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eiOjbHgr2sb18md+SsAMWXaVDlyWVjaqACqBD15vMd4oNHYkk5reHekXgrerVRYanTIszWooAQ91hqmtzqe4ew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('D5SxLv1HUsD7iT26uECK/dZwVwwUfiO41+a/sDy+OrFdg2RmFvZWG+ds2HNZ1ZC+Pdd1negAFB2iSpcSrHazFA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4495290.Kelli_Sullivan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1292269909p3/4495290.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3987580382015983576">Kelli (Kiki) Sullivan was born in Ottawa, Ontario Canada. She has traveled the globe extensively and lived abroad. She enjoys the outdoors and all sports, her favorite being hockey. She is a history and war buff, and loves to work on genealogy in her spare time. She started working in television when she was only 16 years old, where she was the recipient of several television production awards, an</span>
  <span id="freeText3987580382015983576" style="display:none">Kelli (Kiki) Sullivan was born in Ottawa, Ontario Canada. She has traveled the globe extensively and lived abroad. She enjoys the outdoors and all sports, her favorite being hockey. She is a history and war buff, and loves to work on genealogy in her spare time. She started working in television when she was only 16 years old, where she was the recipient of several television production awards, and since then held a variety of positions in various fields. <br /><br />As a child Kelli Sullivan dreamed of being two things. The first was a professional hockey player, and the second was a hobo. When asked why a hobo? Kelli Sullivan responded with " when I was a kid I loved the Canadian television show called “ The Littlest Hobo”. It was about a dog, that wandered around the country helping people in need. I always thought it would be interesting to just wander around experiencing life. I suppose I have taken that show literally".<br /><br />Kelli Sullivan considers herself a lost soul. She doesn't like to stay in one place or one profession for to long, she feels the need to experience all that life has to offer and tends to move on after a position has lost it's challenge for her. <br /><br />After years of extensive traveling and career changing she decided to start writing for the fun of it.<br /><br />Her first novel "Ice In My Veins" is an inspirational novel for anyone who is afraid to chase their dreams.<br /><br />"Rocket to the Moon" is a children's story about using your imagination. <br /><br />She is also a published Poet and won an editor's choice award for her poem “Caves”.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3987580382015983576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
